The Philosophers' View on Agent in Mixture and Its Refutation
Explains philosophers' view on agency in mixture, objection, and two refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how philosophers explain agency in elemental mixture, the objection raised against their view, and the two-fold refutation that resolves the logical difficulty.

Core Idea
In mixture, forms act through qualities, but the real agency is from the separate principle.

This passage delves into the third point of a larger discussion on elemental mixture. It contrasts the medical and philosophical perspectives, explains why the agent must be form rather than matter or quality alone, presents a key objection about simultaneous dominance, and then offers two subtle refutations. Understanding this intricate argument clarifies the philosophical framework of causality and preparation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish medical and philosophical views
Note that physicians only recognize four qualities (hot, cold, wet, dry) as agents, while philosophers also affirm substantial forms. Read the opening lines to see this contrast.
The philosophers' view builds on proofs for forms mentioned earlier.
2
Understand why form is the agent
The passage argues that neither matter (passive) nor quality alone (logically problematic) can be the agent. The form acts through its essential or accidental quality, transforming the other element's matter by 'breaking' the dominance of its quality.
The term 'sūra' here means 'dominance/intensity', not 'form'.
3
Grasp the objection about interaction of forms via qualities
An objector claims that the same problem occurs for forms: if two forms interact via qualities, either simultaneously (impossible) or sequentially (also impossible). Focus on why simultaneous interaction entails coexistence of intense and weak qualities in one moment.
The author of al-Mawāqif restricts himself to the simultaneous case for brevity.
4
Explore the first refutation: metaphorical agency
The first response denies that forms are direct agents; they are merely preparations for the emanation of the intermediate quality from a separate principle (the Active Intellect or God). Thus the issue of dominance disappears.
This refutation aligns with both philosophical and theological frameworks (habit vs. necessary concomitance).
5
Explore the second refutation: breaking of dominance, not essence
The second response clarifies that what is broken in mixture is the 'dominance' (sūra) of a quality, not the quality itself. The breaker is the opposite quality itself. This allows a quality to be both broken and breaking without contradiction.
Example: hot water's intensity is broken by cold water, even if the cold water is not extremely cold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: أن عند امتزاج العناصر الفاعل والمنفعل، هي الكيفيات الأربع في نظر الطبيب، إذ لا ثبت عنده للصور النوعية . وأما الفلاسفة فلما أثبتوها بما سبق من الأدلة جعلوا الفاعل هو الصورة بتوسط الكيفية التي لمادتها بالذات، كحرارة النار، أو بالعرض كحرارة الماء، ومعنى فاعليتها أن تحيل مادة العنصر الآخر إلى كيفيتها، فتكسر سورة كيفية الآخر بمعنى أن تزول تلك المرتبة من مراتب تلك الكيفية، وتحدث مرتبة أخرى أضعف منها . أما كون الفاعل هو الصورة فلأنه لا يجوز أن يكون هو المادة لأن شأنها القبول والانفعال ولا الكيفية لأن تفاعل الكيفيتين أي كسر كل منهما سورة الأخرى، إن كان معاً لزم أن يكون الشيء مغلوباً عن شيء حال كونه غالباً عليه، وإن كان على التعاقب، بأن تكسر سورة الأخرى، ثم ينكسر عنها، لزم أن يصير المغلوب عن الشيء غالباً عليه، والغالب على الشيء مغلوباً عنه ، وذلك أن المنكسر عندما كان قوياً لم يقو على كسر الآخر، فلما انكسر وضعفت قوته قوي على كسر الآخر وهذا محال ، وأما توسط الكيفية فلأن منشأ الكسر والانكسار هو التضاد وذلك في الكيفيات، ولهذا لا تكسر سورة الهواء البارد برودة الأرض، ولا سورة الماء الحار حرارة الهواء ونحو ذلك . واعترض بأن ما ذكر مشترك الإلزام، لأن تفاعل الصورتين بواسطة الكيفيتين، إما أن يكون معاً فيلزم كون الشيء غالباً مغلوباً معاً ، لأن الكيفية كما أنها غالبة إذا فرضناها الكاسرة، فكذا إذا كان لها دخل في ذلك بل يلزم اجتماع الكيفية الشديدة التي بها الكسر ، والضعيفة الحادثة بالانكسار في آن واحد، وهو محال لأنهما مرتبتان مختلفتان وإما أن يكون على التعاقب فتلزم صيرورة المغلوب غالباً وبالعكس ، ولظهور بطلان هذا، ولزوم كون المعلول مقارناً للعلة وشرطها، اقتصر في المواقف على الشق الأول . فقال : الصورة إنما تفعل بواسطة الكيفية، فتكون الكيفية شرطاً في التأثير فيلزم اجتماع الكيفية الكاسرة. أي التي بواسطتها الكسر مع الحادثة أي الضعيفة التي تحدث بعد الانكسار. لا يقال الاعتراض مدفوع بوجهين : أحدهما : أن القول بفاعلية الصورة تجوز والحقيقة أن الصور والكيفيات معدات لفيضان الكيفية المتوسطة من المبدأ المفارق بطريق اللزوم عند الفلاسفة لتمام الفاعل والقابل وبطريق العادة عند غيرهم لكون الفاعل مختاراً، وحينئذ يبطل حديث الغالب والمغلوب . وثانيهما: أن المنكسر عند الامتزاج من كل كيفية سورتها لا نفسها، والكاسر نفس الكيفية المضادة لا سورتها للقطع بأن سورة الماء الشديد الحرارة تنكسر بالماء البارد، وإن لم يكن في الغاية، بل بالماء الفاتر، بل بماء حار هو أقل حرارة ، وإذا كان كذلك، فلا يمتنع أن تكون الكيفية المنكسرة كاسرة لسورة الكيفية المضادة، ولا يكون هذا من اجتماع الغالبية والمغلوبية في شيء لأن نقول : فحينئذ يصح القول بتفاعل الكيفيات من غير اعتبار للصور.
The third: That when mixing the elements, the agent and the patient are the four qualities in the view of the physician, since he does not affirm specific forms. As for the philosophers, since they affirmed them by the preceding proofs, they made the agent the form (al-ṣūra) mediated by the quality (al-kayfiyya) which belongs to its matter essentially, like the heat of fire, or accidentally, like the heat of water. And the meaning of its agency is that it transforms the matter of the other element to its quality, so it breaks the dominance (sūra) of the other quality, meaning that that degree of the degrees of that quality disappears, and another weaker degree occurs. As for the form being the agent, it is because it is not permissible that it be the matter, for its role is reception and passivity; nor the quality, because the interaction of the two qualities—i.e., each breaking the dominance of the other—if simultaneous, it would necessitate that a thing be overcome by something while being dominant over it; and if sequential, by one breaking the dominance of the other, then being broken by it, it would necessitate that the overcome become dominant over the thing, and the dominant become overcome by it, because the broken, when it was strong, did not have the power to break the other, then when it broke and its strength weakened, it became strong enough to break the other—and this is impossible. As for the mediation of the quality, it is because the source of breaking and being broken is opposition, and that is in the qualities; hence the dominance of cold air is not broken by the coldness of the earth, nor the dominance of hot water by the heat of air, and so on. And an objection was raised: that what was mentioned is a common binding implication, because the interaction of the two forms via the two qualities—either it is simultaneous, necessitating that a thing be both dominant and overcome together, since the quality, just as it is dominant if we suppose it to be the breaker, so too if it has a role in that; rather, it necessitates the conjunction of the intense quality by which the breaking occurs and the weak quality that occurs after the breaking in one moment, which is impossible because they are two different degrees; or it is sequential, necessitating the transformation of the overcome into the dominant and vice versa. And because of the obvious falsity of this, and the necessity that the effect be simultaneous with its cause and its condition, [the author of] al-Mawāqif restricted himself to the first branch. So he said: The form only acts through the mediation of the quality, so the quality is a condition in the effect, necessitating the conjunction of the breaking quality—i.e. that by which the breaking occurs—with the occurring quality, i.e. the weak one that arises after the breaking. It is not said: the objection is refuted in two ways. One: The statement of the agency of the form is metaphorical, and the reality is that forms and qualities are preparations (mu‘iddāt) for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle (al-mabda’ al-mufāriq) by way of necessary concomitance (bi-ṭarīq al-luzūm) according to the philosophers for the completion of the agent and the recipient, and by way of habit (bi-ṭarīq al-‘āda) according to others because the agent is free; thereby the talk of dominant and overcome becomes invalid. Two: What is broken in mixture of each quality is its dominance (sūratuhā), not itself, and the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its dominance, for it is certain that the dominance of water of intense heat is broken by cold water, even if it is not extreme, rather by lukewarm water, even by hot water that is less hot. And if this is so, then it is not impossible for the broken quality to be the breaker of the dominance of the opposite quality, and this is not at all from the conjunction of dominance and being overcome because we say: Then it is valid to say that qualities interact without considering forms.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents the third point of a larger discussion on mixture of elements. It first contrasts the medical view, which recognizes only the four primary qualities (hot, cold, wet, dry), with the philosophical view that adds substantial forms as agents. The philosophers argue that the agent in mixture is the form (e.g., the form of fire) acting through its quality (heat). The form transforms the other element's matter, 'breaking' the dominance or intensity of its quality.

The author then explains why the agent cannot be matter (which is passive) or quality alone: if two qualities interact directly, they would either break each other simultaneously—requiring a thing to be both dominant and overcome at once—or sequentially, which would require a weaker thing to later overcome a stronger one, both absurd.

An objection is raised: the same problem applies to forms acting through qualities. The response (from al-Mawāqif) considers only the simultaneous case: the form acts through quality, so the breaking quality and the newly formed weak quality coexist, which seems impossible.

The objection is then refuted in two ways. First, the attribution of agency to forms is metaphorical; in reality, forms and qualities are merely preparations for the emanation of the intermediate quality from a separate principle (God or the Active Intellect), so the whole issue of dominance and being overcome disappears. Second, in mixture, what is broken is not the quality itself but its 'sūra' (intensity/dominance), while the breaker is the opposite quality itself. For example, the dominance of very hot water is broken by cold water, even if the cold water is not extremely cold. Thus, a broken quality can simultaneously break the dominance of its opposite without logical contradiction, allowing for pure interaction of qualities without need for forms.

Key Terms
صورة (form)
كيفية (quality)
سورة (dominance/intensity)
امتزاج (mixture)
فاعل (agent)
منفعل (patient)
مبدأ مفارق (separate principle)
إعداد (preparation)
كسر (breaking)
انكسار (being broken)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers' view of agency in mixture involves direct interaction of forms without qualification, leading to logical impossibility.
Correction: The passage clarifies that forms act through qualities, and the objection is resolved by either metaphorical agency (preparation for emanation) or by distinguishing dominance from essence, allowing qualities to interact without forms needing to be simultaneous agents.

Checkpoint
According to the first refutation, what is the role of forms and qualities in mixture?
A) They are direct agents.
B) They are preparations for emanation from a separate principle.
C) They are irrelevant.
D) They are passive recipients.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' view on agency in mixture is defended by two refutations: one reinterprets agency as metaphorical preparation, the other distinguishes between a quality and its intensity, allowing reciprocal interaction without contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a physical cause produce an effect—like fire heating water—do you unconsciously assume the fire itself is the true agent, or do you remember that it is only a preparation for Allah's direct creation of the heat? How does this lesson's first refutation challenge your default thinking?
?
The philosophers distinguish between a quality and its dominance (sūra). In your own life, can you separate your actions from their perceived strength or intensity? Are you more attached to the dominance of your deeds (e.g., the impression they make) than to the deeds themselves as mere preparations?
?
If all created causes are only preparations for the true Agent's action, how should that change the way you rely on means and strategies in your daily affairs? What practical steps can you take today to shift your trust from apparent causes to the Real Cause?

Second Objection: Observed Quality Interaction Without Form
Raises a second objection: observed quality change does not require a form, and the response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection against the necessity of a form for quality change and the philosophical response that invokes preparedness and emanation.

Core Idea
Quality change can occur without a breaking form, as seen in mixing hot and cold water.

This lesson presents a second objection to the philosophers' claim that a form is needed to break the dominance of a quality. Using the everyday example of mixing hot and cold water, the objector argues that the intermediate quality arises directly from interaction, not from a form. The philosophers counter by appealing to preparedness and emanation. Let's examine the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully. Note how the example of mixing hot and cold water shows that an intermediate quality (lukewarm) arises without any form breaking the dominance of either quality.
The watery form is the same in both waters and does not break coldness.
2
Identify the philosophical response
Identify how the philosophers concede that there is no literal 'breaking' but reinterpret the process: the combination prepares the matter, and the new quality emanates from the emanative principle.
The response preserves the philosophical framework by attributing the new quality to a higher cause.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this objection challenges the necessity of forms for quality changes and how the response maintains the role of a transcendent cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وههنا اعتراض آخر وهو أنا نجد حدوث الكيفية المتوسطة بمجرد تفاعل الكيفيات من غير اعتبار أن يكون هناك صورة توجب انكسار سورة الكيفية المضادة، كما في امتزاج الماء الحار بالماء البارد للقطع بأن الصورة المائية، لا تكسر البرودة . فإن زعموا : أن ليس ههنا فعل وانفعال، أي كسر وانكسار، ليلزم وجود صورة كاسرة ، بل تستعد المادة بواسطة اجتماع المائين لزوال كيفيتهما، وحدوث كيفية متوسطة من المبدأ الفياض.
And here is another objection: that we find the occurrence of the intermediate quality simply from the interaction of qualities, without considering that there be a form that necessitates the breaking of the dominance of the opposite quality, as in the mixture of hot water with cold water, for it is certain that the watery form does not break the coldness. For if they claim that there is here no action and passion, i.e., breaking and being broken, necessitating the existence of a breaking form, but rather the matter is prepared through the combination of the two waters for the removal of their two qualities and the occurrence of an intermediate quality from the emanative principle (al-mabda’ al-fayyāḍ).
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage introduces a second objection against the philosophers' view that a form is needed to break the dominance of a quality. The objector points to everyday experience: mixing hot and cold water produces lukewarm water. Here, the watery form is the same in both waters, and it does not 'break' coldness; rather, the qualities interact directly. Thus, no form is required to act as a breaker.

The response (attributed to the philosophers) concedes that there is no 'breaking' in the literal sense; instead, the two waters combine, and the matter is prepared (tasta‘idd) by their conjunction for the removal of both original qualities and the generation of a new intermediate quality—not through the action of a form, but through emanation from the 'emanative principle' (al-mabda’ al-fayyāḍ, i.e., God or the Active Intellect). This preserves the philosophical framework by attributing the new quality to a higher cause, while acknowledging that the forms themselves do not directly produce the effect in this case.

Key Terms
كيفية متوسطة (intermediate quality)
تفاعل (interaction)
صورة مائية (watery form)
استعداد (preparedness)
مبدأ فياض (emanative principle)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the philosophers deny observed quality changes; they instead reinterpret them as preparations for emanation from a separate principle.
Correction: The philosophers do not deny the change; they explain it via preparedness and emanation from a higher cause.

First Objection: Conjunction of Qualities and Two Answers
Al-Taftazani refutes the first objection against forms in mixture with two answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection against the role of forms in mixture and the two answers provided by al-Taftazani.

Core Idea
Forms are instruments; what breaks is intensity, not quality itself.

The author begins by addressing a crucial objection: if qualities interact, how can a breaking quality coexist with the broken quality? He provides two sophisticated replies that distinguish between the quality itself and its intensity, and reframe the role of forms as instrumental.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answers
Read the passage to understand the objection and the two answers presented.
Pay attention to the structure: objection, then first answer, then second answer.
2
Understand the first answer
The first answer states that forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle. This removes the need for direct breaking.
The philosophers view this as by concomitance; theologians see it as by habit due to a free agent.
3
Understand the second answer
The second answer distinguishes between the quality and its intensity. What breaks is the quality itself, not its intensity, so there is no contradiction.
Example: very hot water's intensity breaks with cold or less hot water.

الكيفية، فتكون الكيفية(1) شرطاً في التأثير فيلزم اجتماع الكيفية الكاسرة. أي التي بواسطتها الكسر مع الحادثة أي الضعيفة التي تحدث بعد الانكسار. لا يقال الاعتراض مدفوع بوجهين : أحدهما : أن القول بفاعلية الصورة تجوز والحقيقة أن الصور والكيفيات معدات لفيضان الكيفية المتوسطة من المبدأ المفارق بطريق اللزوم (2) عند الفلاسفة لتمام الفاعل والقابل وبطريق العادة عند غيرهم لكون الفاعل مختاراً، وحينئذ يبطل حديث (3) الغالب والمغلوب . وثانيهما: أن المنكسر عند الامتزاج من كل كيفية سورتها لا نفسها، والكاسر نفس الكيفية المضادة لا سورتها للقطع بأن سورة الماء الشديد الحرارة تنكسر بالماء البارد، وإن لم يكن في يصح القول بتفاعل الكيفيات من غير اعتبار للصور. وههنا اعتراض آخر وهو أنا نجد حدوث الكيفية المتوسطة بمجرد تفاعل الكيفيات من غير اعتبار (4) أن يكون هناك صورة توجب انكسار سورة (5) الكيفية المضادة، كما في وإنما النزاع في الفاعل، وإن زعموا أن الكاسر لسورة برودة الماء الصورة النارية التي أحدثت الحرارة في الماء الحار. هو قلنا : فقد ظهر أنه ليس بلازم أن يكون الكاسر للكيفية صورة بسيط هو أحد أجزاء المركب. فبطل قولكم في المزاج ، بأن انكسار الكيفيات، إنما هو بصور عناصر الممتزج ، ثم الأشبه أن يقال: الكاسر السورة برودة الماء البارد المختلط ، أن بالماء الحار هو الصورة المائية بتوسط الحرارة العارضة. لأن من قواعدهم صورة كل عنصر تفعل في مادته بالذات، وفي مجاوره بواسطة الكيفية ذاتية كانت كبرودة الماء، أو عرضية كحرارته فعلية كالحرارة والبرودة (3) ، أو انفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة ، ومادة كل عنصر تنفعل بالذات عن صورته وتكيفيته الذاتية أو العرضية الفعلية والانفعالية عن مجاورة، وعلى هذا لا يرد على القائلين يكون الفاعل هو الصورة ما يرد على القائلين بكونه هو الكيفية من لزوم انفعال الكيفية الفعلية، فيما إذا كان وكما لا يمتنع انفعالها في الكيفية الفعلية كالحرارة والبرودة لا يمتنع فعل الصورة بالكيفية الانفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة ، للقطع بأن صورة الماء مثلاً إنما تكسر يبوسة (1) النار برطوبته لا ببرودته،
the quality, so the quality becomes a condition in the effect, and thus there would be a conjunction of the breaking quality—that by which breaking occurs—with the occurring one, i.e., the weak one that comes into existence after the breaking. It is not said that the objection is repelled by two aspects: One: that the statement that the form is an agent is a metaphor, and the truth is that forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle by way of concomitance (al-luzum) according to the philosophers, for the completion of the agent and the recipient, and by way of habit according to others, because the agent is free. And then the talk of the dominant and the dominated becomes invalid. And the second: that that which is broken in mixture from each quality is its intensity (suratuhā), not itself, and the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its intensity, because it is certain that the intensity of very hot water is broken by cold water, even if not at the extreme, but by lukewarm water, even by hot water that is less hot. And if this is so, then it is not impossible for the broken quality to be the breaker of the intensity of the opposite quality, and this does not involve the conjunction of dominance and being dominated at all, because we say: then it is valid to say that qualities interact without considering forms. And here is another objection: that we find the occurrence of the intermediate quality by mere interaction of qualities without considering that there is a form that necessitates the breaking of the intensity of the opposite quality, as in the mixture of hot water with cold water, because it is certain that the water form does not break coldness. For if they claim that there is no action and passion here, i.e., breaking and being broken, so that the existence of a breaking form would be necessary, but rather the matter becomes prepared by the conjunction of the two waters for the removal of their two qualities and the occurrence of an intermediate quality from the emanating principle. We say: Then let the matter in the mixture also be like that. For there is no meaning of intensification and weakening of a quality except the nullification of a quality and the occurrence of another stronger or weaker according to the difference of preparedness, and the dispute is only about the agent. And if they claim that the breaker of the intensity of the coldness of water is the fire form that produced heat in the hot water. We say: Then it has become evident that it is not necessary for the breaker of the quality to be a simple form that is one of the parts of the compound. So your statement in the mixture that the breaking of qualities is only by the forms of the elements of the mixture is invalidated. Then the more appropriate is to say that the breaker of the intensity of the coldness of the cold water mixed with the hot water is the water form by means of the accidental heat. Because it is among their rules that the form of each element acts in its matter essentially, and in its neighbor by means of a quality, whether intrinsic like the coldness of water, or accidental like its heat, active like heat and cold, or passive like moisture and dryness, and the matter of each element is affected essentially by its form and its intrinsic or accidental qualities, active and passive, from the neighbor. And on this, what is directed against those who say the agent is the form does not occur as what is directed against those who say it is the quality, regarding the necessity of the affection of the active quality when the breaking and being broken are between the two active ones, namely heat and cold, and the necessity of the activeness of the passive quality when the breaking and being broken are between the two passive ones, namely moisture and dryness. For if it is said: if there is obscurity in the agency, there is no obscurity in the fact that the passive object in mixture is the qualities like the heat of fire and the coldness of water, and likewise the rest. We say: Yes, in the sense that they perish and the intermediate quality occurs. But that which is affected and changes from state to state is matter alone. And just as it is not impossible for it to be affected in the active quality like heat and cold, it is not impossible for the form to act by the passive quality like moisture and dryness, because it is certain that the form of water, for example, breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a sequence of objections and answers concerning the interaction of qualities in mixture (imtizāj). The author, al-Taftazani, is discussing whether the agent (fāʿil) in the production of an intermediate quality (kayfiyya mutawassiṭa) is the form (ṣūra) or the quality itself, and whether forms are needed as breakers of opposing qualities.

First, an objection is raised: if qualities interact directly, then the breaking quality would have to be present at the same time as the broken quality, leading to a conjunction of contradictory intensities. The author gives two replies. The first reply is that the claim that forms are agents is a metaphor; in reality, forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle (al-mabdaʾ al-mufāriq). For philosophers, this is by way of concomitance (luzūm) when agent and recipient are complete; for others (theologians), it is by way of habit (ʿāda) because the agent is free. Thus the talk of dominance and being dominated becomes irrelevant. The second reply is that in mixture, what is broken is the intensity (sūra) of a quality, not the quality itself, while the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its intensity. He gives the example of very hot water being broken by cold water, lukewarm water, or even less hot water. Hence the broken quality can break the intensity of the opposite quality without contradiction.

Then another objection is presented: we observe the occurrence of an intermediate quality by mere interaction of qualities, like hot and cold water mixing, without any form breaking the coldness. The opponent might claim that there is no acting and being acted upon (breaking and being broken) at all; rather, the matter becomes prepared by the conjunction of the two waters for the removal of their qualities and the emanation of an intermediate quality from the Emanating Principle (al-mabdaʾ al-fayyāḍ). The author replies: then let the same be said for mixture (mizāj) as well—intensification and weakening are nothing but the nullification of one quality and occurrence of another according to preparedness, and the dispute is only about the agent. If they claim the breaker is the fire form that caused heat, the author responds that it is not necessary that the breaker be a simple form that is part of the compound; rather, it could be the water form via the accidental heat. He then explains the rule: the form of each element acts essentially in its own matter, and in its neighbor by means of a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive). The matter is affected essentially by its form and by neighboring qualities. This avoids the problems faced by those who say the agent is the quality: if breaking is between two active qualities (heat and cold), there would be affection of the active quality; if between two passive qualities (moisture and dryness), the passive quality would need to be active. The author's account avoids these.

Finally, a last objection: there is no doubt that the passive object in mixture is the qualities themselves. The author concedes that qualities perish and the intermediate quality occurs, but the true patient (that which is affected and changes) is matter alone. Just as matter can be affected in active qualities, it can be affected by the form acting through passive qualities, e.g., the water form breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness.

Key Terms
كيفية (kayfiyya)
صورة (ṣūra)
امتزاج (imtizāj)
كسر (kasr)
انكسار (inkisār)
كيفية متوسطة (kayfiyya mutawassiṭa)
مبدأ مفارق (mabdaʾ mufāriq)
سورة (sūra, intensity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first answer, what is the true source of the intermediate quality?
A) The breaking quality itself
B) The form of the element
C) The separate principle (al-mabdaʾ al-mufāriq)
D) The mixture of qualities

Key Takeaway
The first objection is answered by distinguishing the role of forms as instruments and separating the quality from its intensity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience spiritual 'weakness' or 'cooling' of faith, do you think your faith itself (the quality) is broken or only its intensity? How does this lesson's distinction change the way you understand and respond to such moments?
?
Al-Taftazani says that forms and qualities are merely instruments for the separate principle. In your daily actions, do you tend to see your own efforts as the ultimate cause, or as instruments through which God works? What would change if you truly saw yourself as a muʿidd (instrument)?
?
The objection assumes that a breaking quality and a broken quality cannot coexist. Is there a relationship in your life where you struggle to hold two seemingly opposite states (like justice and mercy, or humility and confidence)? How might the distinction between quality and intensity help you navigate that tension without contradiction?

Second Objection: Mere Interaction Without Forms
Al-Taftazani addresses the second objection about the absence of forms in observable mixture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection against forms and the author's initial response that the dispute is about the agent.

Core Idea
The observable interaction is not the dispute; the agent is the key.

A second objection seems stronger: we observe hot and cold water mixing without any form breaking coldness. The author responds by shifting the debate to the nature of the agent and showing that the same principle underlies all qualitative change.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objection claims that the intermediate quality arises from mere interaction of qualities without any form, using the example of hot and cold water.
The water form is said not to break coldness.
2
Understand the opponent's alternative
The opponent may claim there is no breaking at all; rather, matter becomes prepared for emanation from the Emanating Principle.
This removes the need for a breaking form.
3
Grasp the author's reply
The author replies that the same can be said for any mixture; the real dispute is about the agent, not the observable interaction.
He also refutes the claim that the breaker must be a simple form part of the compound.

الكيفية، فتكون الكيفية(1) شرطاً في التأثير فيلزم اجتماع الكيفية الكاسرة. أي التي بواسطتها الكسر مع الحادثة أي الضعيفة التي تحدث بعد الانكسار. لا يقال الاعتراض مدفوع بوجهين : أحدهما : أن القول بفاعلية الصورة تجوز والحقيقة أن الصور والكيفيات معدات لفيضان الكيفية المتوسطة من المبدأ المفارق بطريق اللزوم (2) عند الفلاسفة لتمام الفاعل والقابل وبطريق العادة عند غيرهم لكون الفاعل مختاراً، وحينئذ يبطل حديث (3) الغالب والمغلوب . وثانيهما: أن المنكسر عند الامتزاج من كل كيفية سورتها لا نفسها، والكاسر نفس الكيفية المضادة لا سورتها للقطع بأن سورة الماء الشديد الحرارة تنكسر بالماء البارد، وإن لم يكن في الغاية، بل بالماء الفاتر، بل بماء حار هو أقل حرارة ، وإذا كان كذلك، فلا يمتنع أن تكون الكيفية المنكسرة كاسرة لسورة الكيفية المضادة، ولا يكون هذا من اجتماع الغالبية والمغلوبية في شيء لأن نقول : فحينئذ يصح القول بتفاعل الكيفيات من غير اعتبار للصور. وههنا اعتراض آخر وهو أنا نجد حدوث الكيفية المتوسطة بمجرد تفاعل الكيفيات من غير اعتبار (4) أن يكون هناك صورة توجب انكسار سورة (5) الكيفية المضادة، كما في امتزاج الماء الحار بالماء البارد للقطع بأن الصورة المائية، لا تكسر البرودة . فإن زعموا : أن ليس ههنا فعل وانفعال، أي كسر وانكسار، ليلزم وجود صورة كاسرة ، بل تستعد المادة بواسطة اجتماع المائين لزوال كيفيتهما، وحدوث كيفية متوسطة من المبدأ الفياض. قلنا: فليكن الأمر في المزاج أيضاً (1) كذلك. فأنه لا معنى لاشتداد الكيفية وضعفها إلا بطلان ،كيفية، وحدوث أخرى أشد منها أو أضعف بحسب اختلاف (2) الاستعداد، وإنما النزاع في الفاعل، وإن زعموا أن الكاسر لسورة برودة الماء الصورة النارية التي أحدثت الحرارة في الماء الحار. هو قلنا : فقد ظهر أنه ليس بلازم أن يكون الكاسر للكيفية صورة بسيط هو أحد أجزاء المركب. فبطل قولكم في المزاج ، بأن انكسار الكيفيات، إنما هو بصور عناصر الممتزج ، ثم الأشبه أن يقال: الكاسر السورة برودة الماء البارد المختلط ، أن بالماء الحار هو الصورة المائية بتوسط الحرارة العارضة. لأن من قواعدهم صورة كل عنصر تفعل في مادته بالذات، وفي مجاوره بواسطة الكيفية ذاتية كانت كبرودة الماء، أو عرضية كحرارته فعلية كالحرارة والبرودة (3) ، أو انفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة ، ومادة كل عنصر تنفعل بالذات عن صورته وتكيفيته الذاتية أو العرضية الفعلية والانفعالية عن مجاورة، وعلى هذا لا يرد على القائلين يكون الفاعل هو الصورة ما يرد على القائلين بكونه هو الكيفية من لزوم انفعال الكيفية الفعلية، فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الفعليتين، أعني الحرارة (4) والبرودة ، ولزوم فعلية الكيفية الانفعالية، فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الانفعاليين. أعني الرطوبة واليبوسة فإن قيل : إن كان في الفاعلية خفاء، فلا خفاء في أن المنفعل عند الامتزاج هو الكيفيات كحرارة النار وبرودة الماء، وكذا البواقي (م) (0) قلنا : نعم بمعنى أنها تزول، وتحدث الكيفية المتوسطة، وأما الذي يتأثر ويتغير من حال إلى حال فهو المادة لا غير وكما لا يمتنع انفعالها في الكيفية الفعلية كالحرارة والبرودة لا يمتنع فعل الصورة بالكيفية الانفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة ، للقطع بأن صورة الماء مثلاً إنما تكسر يبوسة (1) النار برطوبته لا ببرودته،
the quality, so the quality becomes a condition in the effect, and thus there would be a conjunction of the breaking quality—that by which breaking occurs—with the occurring one, i.e., the weak one that comes into existence after the breaking. It is not said that the objection is repelled by two aspects: One: that the statement that the form is an agent is a metaphor, and the truth is that forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle by way of concomitance (al-luzum) according to the philosophers, for the completion of the agent and the recipient, and by way of habit according to others, because the agent is free. And then the talk of the dominant and the dominated becomes invalid. And the second: that that which is broken in mixture from each quality is its intensity (suratuhā), not itself, and the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its intensity, because it is certain that the intensity of very hot water is broken by cold water, even if not at the extreme, but by lukewarm water, even by hot water that is less hot. And if this is so, then it is not impossible for the broken quality to be the breaker of the intensity of the opposite quality, and this does not involve the conjunction of dominance and being dominated at all, because we say: then it is valid to say that qualities interact without considering forms. And here is another objection: that we find the occurrence of the intermediate quality by mere interaction of qualities without considering that there is a form that necessitates the breaking of the intensity of the opposite quality, as in the mixture of hot water with cold water, because it is certain that the water form does not break coldness. For if they claim that there is no action and passion here, i.e., breaking and being broken, so that the existence of a breaking form would be necessary, but rather the matter becomes prepared by the conjunction of the two waters for the removal of their two qualities and the occurrence of an intermediate quality from the emanating principle. We say: Then let the matter in the mixture also be like that. For there is no meaning of intensification and weakening of a quality except the nullification of a quality and the occurrence of another stronger or weaker according to the difference of preparedness, and the dispute is only about the agent. And if they claim that the breaker of the intensity of the coldness of water is the fire form that produced heat in the hot water. We say: Then it has become evident that it is not necessary for the breaker of the quality to be a simple form that is one of the parts of the compound. So your statement in the mixture that the breaking of qualities is only by the forms of the elements of the mixture is invalidated. Then the more appropriate is to say that the breaker of the intensity of the coldness of the cold water mixed with the hot water is the water form by means of the accidental heat. Because it is among their rules that the form of each element acts in its matter essentially, and in its neighbor by means of a quality, whether intrinsic like the coldness of water, or accidental like its heat, active like heat and cold, or passive like moisture and dryness, and the matter of each element is affected essentially by its form and its intrinsic or accidental qualities, active and passive, from the neighbor. And on this, what is directed against those who say the agent is the form does not occur as what is directed against those who say it is the quality, regarding the necessity of the affection of the active quality when the breaking and being broken are between the two active ones, namely heat and cold, and the necessity of the activeness of the passive quality when the breaking and being broken are between the two passive ones, namely moisture and dryness. For if it is said: if there is obscurity in the agency, there is no obscurity in the fact that the passive object in mixture is the qualities like the heat of fire and the coldness of water, and likewise the rest. We say: Yes, in the sense that they perish and the intermediate quality occurs. But that which is affected and changes from state to state is matter alone. And just as it is not impossible for it to be affected in the active quality like heat and cold, it is not impossible for the form to act by the passive quality like moisture and dryness, because it is certain that the form of water, for example, breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness.

Commentary
This passage is a sequence of objections and answers concerning the interaction of qualities in mixture (imtizāj). The author, al-Taftazani, is discussing whether the agent (fāʿil) in the production of an intermediate quality (kayfiyya mutawassiṭa) is the form (ṣūra) or the quality itself, and whether forms are needed as breakers of opposing qualities.

First, an objection is raised: if qualities interact directly, then the breaking quality would have to be present at the same time as the broken quality, leading to a conjunction of contradictory intensities. The author gives two replies. The first reply is that the claim that forms are agents is a metaphor; in reality, forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle (al-mabdaʾ al-mufāriq). For philosophers, this is by way of concomitance (luzūm) when agent and recipient are complete; for others (theologians), it is by way of habit (ʿāda) because the agent is free. Thus the talk of dominance and being dominated becomes irrelevant. The second reply is that in mixture, what is broken is the intensity (sūra) of a quality, not the quality itself, while the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its intensity. He gives the example of very hot water being broken by cold water, lukewarm water, or even less hot water. Hence the broken quality can break the intensity of the opposite quality without contradiction.

Then another objection is presented: we observe the occurrence of an intermediate quality by mere interaction of qualities, like hot and cold water mixing, without any form breaking the coldness. The opponent might claim that there is no acting and being acted upon (breaking and being broken) at all; rather, the matter becomes prepared by the conjunction of the two waters for the removal of their qualities and the emanation of an intermediate quality from the Emanating Principle (al-mabdaʾ al-fayyāḍ). The author replies: then let the same be said for mixture (mizāj) as well—intensification and weakening are nothing but the nullification of one quality and occurrence of another according to preparedness, and the dispute is only about the agent. If they claim the breaker is the fire form that caused heat, the author responds that it is not necessary that the breaker be a simple form that is part of the compound; rather, it could be the water form via the accidental heat. He then explains the rule: the form of each element acts essentially in its own matter, and in its neighbor by means of a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive). The matter is affected essentially by its form and by neighboring qualities. This avoids the problems faced by those who say the agent is the quality: if breaking is between two active qualities (heat and cold), there would be affection of the active quality; if between two passive qualities (moisture and dryness), the passive quality would need to be active. The author's account avoids these.

Finally, a last objection: there is no doubt that the passive object in mixture is the qualities themselves. The author concedes that qualities perish and the intermediate quality occurs, but the true patient (that which is affected and changes) is matter alone. Just as matter can be affected in active qualities, it can be affected by the form acting through passive qualities, e.g., the water form breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the author denies observable interaction between qualities.
Correction: The author affirms the interaction but argues the agent is the form, not the quality directly.

Checkpoint
What does the author say is the real focus of the dispute in the second objection?
A) Whether qualities interact
B) Whether forms exist
C) The nature of the agent
D) The role of matter

Key Takeaway
The second objection is answered by showing that the observable interaction is not in dispute; what matters is identifying the true agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, when you witness changes—a recovery from illness, a conflict resolved, a door opening—do your thoughts immediately go to the apparent cause (a doctor, a peacemaker, a job opportunity) or to the True Agent behind it? What would it take for you to habitually see Allah’s hand first?
?
This lesson shows that the real dispute is about the agent, not the observable interactions. Are there areas in your heart where you have been treating people, systems, or your own efforts as independent agents, effectively forgetting that Allah alone is the Creator of every effect? How can you actively shift your reliance from those means to the True Agent today?
?
If the 'breaker' of qualities can be a form acting through accidental qualities, then even the things we rely on are merely channels. What are you most afraid of losing? Is it possible that your fear reveals that you have placed your trust in the channel rather than the Source? Will you ask Allah to make your heart depend only on Him?

Preferred Explanation: Forms Acting Through Qualities
Al-Taftazani gives his preferred view on how forms break intensities via qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's preferred explanation that the form acts through qualities (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive) to break opposing intensities, and the final clarification that matter is the true patient.

Core Idea
Forms act through qualities; matter is the real subject of change.

Having refuted earlier objections, the author now presents his own account: the water form, via accidental heat or intrinsic coldness, breaks the intensity of the opposite quality. He also clarifies that the real subject of change is matter, not the qualities themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the preferred explanation
The author states that the breaker of the coldness intensity is the water form via accidental heat.
This avoids the need for a simple form as breaker.
2
Understand the rule of forms
The rule: each element's form acts in its own matter essentially and in its neighbor via a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive).
This explains how forms interact without direct action on qualities.
3
Grasp the final clarification
The author addresses a final objection: that the passive object is the qualities themselves. He replies that qualities perish, but the true patient is matter, which can be affected by forms via passive qualities like moisture/dryness.
Example: water form breaks dryness of fire by its moisture, not coldness.

فبطل قولكم في المزاج ، بأن انكسار الكيفيات، إنما هو بصور عناصر الممتزج ، ثم الأشبه أن يقال: الكاسر السورة برودة الماء البارد المختلط ، أن بالماء الحار هو الصورة المائية بتوسط الحرارة العارضة. لأن من قواعدهم صورة كل عنصر تفعل في مادته بالذات، وفي مجاوره بواسطة الكيفية ذاتية كانت كبرودة الماء، أو عرضية كحرارته فعلية كالحرارة والبرودة (3) ، أو انفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة ، ومادة كل عنصر تنفعل بالذات عن صورته وتكيفيته الذاتية أو العرضية الفعلية والانفعالية عن مجاورة، وعلى هذا لا يرد على القائلين يكون الفاعل هو الصورة ما يرد على القائلين بكونه هو الكيفية من لزوم انفعال الكيفية الفعلية، فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الفعليتين، أعني الحرارة (4) والبرودة ، ولزوم فعلية الكيفية الانفعالية، فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الانفعاليين. أعني الرطوبة واليبوسة فإن قيل : إن كان في الفاعلية خفاء، فلا خفاء في أن المنفعل عند الامتزاج هو الكيفيات كحرارة النار وبرودة الماء، وكذا البواقي (م) (0) قلنا : نعم بمعنى أنها تزول، وتحدث الكيفية المتوسطة، وأما الذي يتأثر ويتغير من حال إلى حال فهو المادة لا غير وكما لا يمتنع انفعالها في الكيفية الفعلية كالحرارة والبرودة لا يمتنع فعل الصورة بالكيفية الانفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة ، للقطع بأن صورة الماء مثلاً إنما تكسر يبوسة (1) النار برطوبته لا ببرودته،
the quality, so the quality becomes a condition in the effect, and thus there would be a conjunction of the breaking quality—that by which breaking occurs—with the occurring one, i.e., the weak one that comes into existence after the breaking. It is not said that the objection is repelled by two aspects: One: that the statement that the form is an agent is a metaphor, and the truth is that forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle by way of concomitance (al-luzum) according to the philosophers, for the completion of the agent and the recipient, and by way of habit according to others, because the agent is free. And then the talk of the dominant and the dominated becomes invalid. And the second: that that which is broken in mixture from each quality is its intensity (suratuhā), not itself, and the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its intensity, because it is certain that the intensity of very hot water is broken by cold water, even if not at the extreme, but by lukewarm water, even by hot water that is less hot. And if this is so, then it is not impossible for the broken quality to be the breaker of the intensity of the opposite quality, and this does not involve the conjunction of dominance and being dominated at all, because we say: then it is valid to say that qualities interact without considering forms. And here is another objection: that we find the occurrence of the intermediate quality by mere interaction of qualities without considering that there is a form that necessitates the breaking of the intensity of the opposite quality, as in the mixture of hot water with cold water, because it is certain that the water form does not break coldness. For if they claim that there is no action and passion here, i.e., breaking and being broken, so that the existence of a breaking form would be necessary, but rather the matter becomes prepared by the conjunction of the two waters for the removal of their two qualities and the occurrence of an intermediate quality from the emanating principle. We say: Then let the matter in the mixture also be like that. For there is no meaning of intensification and weakening of a quality except the nullification of a quality and the occurrence of another stronger or weaker according to the difference of preparedness, and the dispute is only about the agent. And if they claim that the breaker of the intensity of the coldness of water is the fire form that produced heat in the hot water. We say: Then it has become evident that it is not necessary for the breaker of the quality to be a simple form that is one of the parts of the compound. So your statement in the mixture that the breaking of qualities is only by the forms of the elements of the mixture is invalidated. Then the more appropriate is to say that the breaker of the intensity of the coldness of the cold water mixed with the hot water is the water form by means of the accidental heat. Because it is among their rules that the form of each element acts in its matter essentially, and in its neighbor by means of a quality, whether intrinsic like the coldness of water, or accidental like its heat, active like heat and cold, or passive like moisture and dryness, and the matter of each element is affected essentially by its form and its intrinsic or accidental qualities, active and passive, from the neighbor. And on this, what is directed against those who say the agent is the form does not occur as what is directed against those who say it is the quality, regarding the necessity of the affection of the active quality when the breaking and being broken are between the two active ones, namely heat and cold, and the necessity of the activeness of the passive quality when the breaking and being broken are between the two passive ones, namely moisture and dryness. For if it is said: if there is obscurity in the agency, there is no obscurity in the fact that the passive object in mixture is the qualities like the heat of fire and the coldness of water, and likewise the rest. We say: Yes, in the sense that they perish and the intermediate quality occurs. But that which is affected and changes from state to state is matter alone. And just as it is not impossible for it to be affected in the active quality like heat and cold, it is not impossible for the form to act by the passive quality like moisture and dryness, because it is certain that the form of water, for example, breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a sequence of objections and answers concerning the interaction of qualities in mixture (imtizāj). The author, al-Taftazani, is discussing whether the agent (fāʿil) in the production of an intermediate quality (kayfiyya mutawassiṭa) is the form (ṣūra) or the quality itself, and whether forms are needed as breakers of opposing qualities.

First, an objection is raised: if qualities interact directly, then the breaking quality would have to be present at the same time as the broken quality, leading to a conjunction of contradictory intensities. The author gives two replies. The first reply is that the claim that forms are agents is a metaphor; in reality, forms and qualities are instruments for the emanation of the intermediate quality from the separate principle (al-mabdaʾ al-mufāriq). For philosophers, this is by way of concomitance (luzūm) when agent and recipient are complete; for others (theologians), it is by way of habit (ʿāda) because the agent is free. Thus the talk of dominance and being dominated becomes irrelevant. The second reply is that in mixture, what is broken is the intensity (sūra) of a quality, not the quality itself, while the breaker is the opposite quality itself, not its intensity. He gives the example of very hot water being broken by cold water, lukewarm water, or even less hot water. Hence the broken quality can break the intensity of the opposite quality without contradiction.

Then another objection is presented: we observe the occurrence of an intermediate quality by mere interaction of qualities, like hot and cold water mixing, without any form breaking the coldness. The opponent might claim that there is no acting and being acted upon (breaking and being broken) at all; rather, the matter becomes prepared by the conjunction of the two waters for the removal of their qualities and the emanation of an intermediate quality from the Emanating Principle (al-mabdaʾ al-fayyāḍ). The author replies: then let the same be said for mixture (mizāj) as well—intensification and weakening are nothing but the nullification of one quality and occurrence of another according to preparedness, and the dispute is only about the agent. If they claim the breaker is the fire form that caused heat, the author responds that it is not necessary that the breaker be a simple form that is part of the compound; rather, it could be the water form via the accidental heat. He then explains the rule: the form of each element acts essentially in its own matter, and in its neighbor by means of a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive). The matter is affected essentially by its form and by neighboring qualities. This avoids the problems faced by those who say the agent is the quality: if breaking is between two active qualities (heat and cold), there would be affection of the active quality; if between two passive qualities (moisture and dryness), the passive quality would need to be active. The author's account avoids these.

Finally, a last objection: there is no doubt that the passive object in mixture is the qualities themselves. The author concedes that qualities perish and the intermediate quality occurs, but the true patient (that which is affected and changes) is matter alone. Just as matter can be affected in active qualities, it can be affected by the form acting through passive qualities, e.g., the water form breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness.

Key Terms
صورة (ṣūra)
كيفية (kayfiyya)
مادة (mādda)
كيفية فعلية (kayfiyya fiʿliyya)
كيفية انفعالية (kayfiyya infiʿāliyya)
رطوبة (ruṭūba)
يبوسة (yubūsa)
فاعل (fāʿil)
منفعل (munfaʿil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the form directly breaks the intensity without involving any quality.
Correction: The form acts through a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive).

Checkpoint
According to the author's rule, through what does the form act in a neighbor?
A) Directly without any medium
B) Through a quality (intrinsic or accidental, active or passive)
C) Only through intrinsic qualities
D) Only through active qualities

Key Takeaway
The preferred view is that forms act through qualities, and matter is the true patient of change in mixture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson argues that when water and fire mix, the water form breaks the dryness of fire by its moisture, not by its coldness. Where in your life are you focusing on superficial qualities (like temperature or mood) rather than the deeper form or essence of a situation? Will you commit today to looking beyond the obvious 'qualities' to the underlying reality?
?
Al-Taftazani insists that matter alone is the true subject of change, while qualities come and go. Think of a recent time you were confused by changing emotions or circumstances. How often do you mistake these passing qualities for your unchanging core? What would it mean to identify with the 'matter' that endures rather than the qualities that perish?
?
The author says that the form acts through qualities to bring about change. Is there a quality in your character—like patience or honesty—that you have treated as the 'agent' itself? Consider that these qualities are merely instruments of a deeper self or spirit. Will you realign your focus onto the form (your soul or intention) rather than the mere quality?

The True Agent in Breaking Qualities: Form, Not Quality
Sanusi refutes that the breaker is a simple form and explains the true agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that the agent that breaks qualities in mixture is the substantial form acting through an accidental quality, not the quality itself.

Core Idea
The form acts through accidental qualities; the matter is the true subject of change.

The debate over mixture among theologians often centers on what actually breaks the qualities of the original elements. Some argue that a simple form (like the form of fire) directly breaks the coldness of water. Sanusi refutes this, proposing instead that the substantial form acts through an accidental quality acquired from the mixing. In this passage, he carefully distinguishes the roles of form, quality, and matter, and addresses a potential objection about the passivity of active qualities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the objection-and-answer structure.
2
Identify the two competing views
Notice the claim that the breaker is a simple form (e.g., fiery form breaking water's coldness) and Sanusi's alternative: the water form breaking coldness via accidental heat.
3
Understand the rules of elemental interaction
Examine the rules Sanusi cites: each element's form acts on its own matter essentially, and on its neighbor through a quality (essential or accidental, active or passive).
These rules are key to answering the objection.
4
See how the passivity objection is resolved
The objection claims that if the agent is the quality, problems arise (active quality becoming passive). Sanusi shows that if the agent is the form acting through a quality, these contradictions disappear.
Focus on the example of water's wetness breaking fire's dryness.
5
Note the final clarification about matter
Sanusi concludes that the qualities vanish, but the true subject of change is the matter, not the qualities themselves.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا: فليكن الأمر في المزاج أيضاً كذلك. فإنه لا معنى لاشتداد الكيفية وضعفها إلا بطلان كيفية وحدوث أخرى أشد منها أو أضعف بحسب اختلاف الاستعداد، وإنما النزاع في الفاعل، وإن زعموا أن الكاسر لسورة برودة الماء الصورة النارية التي أحدثت الحرارة في الماء الحار. هو قلنا: فقد ظهر أنه ليس بلازم أن يكون الكاسر للكيفية صورة بسيط هو أحد أجزاء المركب. فبطل قولكم في المزاج بأن انكسار الكيفيات إنما هو بصور عناصر الممتزج، ثم الأشبه أن يقال: الكاسر لسورة برودة الماء البارد المختلط بالماء الحار هو الصورة المائية بتوسط الحرارة العارضة. لأن من قواعدهم صورة كل عنصر تفعل في مادته بالذات، وفي مجاوره بواسطة الكيفية ذاتية كانت كبرودة الماء أو عرضية كحرارته فعلية كالحرارة والبرودة أو انفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة، ومادة كل عنصر تنفعل بالذات عن صورته وتتكيف بالكيفية الذاتية أو العرضية الفعلية والانفعالية عن مجاورة. وعلى هذا لا يرد على القائلين بأن الفاعل هو الصورة ما يرد على القائلين بكونه هو الكيفية من لزوم انفعال الكيفية الفعلية فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الفعليتين أعني الحرارة والبرودة، ولزوم فعلية الكيفية الانفعالية فيما إذا كان الكسر والانكسار بين الانفعاليين أعني الرطوبة واليبوسة. فإن قيل: إن كان في الفاعلية خفاء فلا خفاء في أن المنفعل عند الامتزاج هو الكيفيات كحرارة النار وبرودة الماء وكذا البواقي. قلنا: نعم بمعنى أنها تزول وتحدث الكيفية المتوسطة، وأما الذي يتأثر ويتغير من حال إلى حال فهو المادة لا غير. وكما لا يمتنع انفعالها في الكيفية الفعلية كالحرارة والبرودة لا يمتنع فعل الصورة بالكيفية الانفعالية كالرطوبة واليبوسة، للقطع بأن صورة الماء مثلاً إنما تكسر يبوسة النار برطوبته لا ببرودته، وصورة النار تكسر رطوبة الماء بيبوستها لا بحرارتها.
We said: So let the matter be likewise in the mixture. For there is no meaning to the intensification and weakening of a quality except the annihilation of a quality and the occurrence of another stronger or weaker according to the difference of preparedness, and the dispute is only concerning the agent, even if they claim that the breaker of the form of the water's coldness is the fiery form which produced heat in the hot water. It is we said: So it has become apparent that it is not necessary that the breaker of the quality be a simple form which is one of the parts of the compound. Therefore your statement regarding mixture has been invalidated that the breaking of qualities is only by the forms of the elements of the mixture. Then the more appropriate is to say: The breaker of the form of the coldness of the cold water mixed with the hot water is the water form through the mediation of the accidental heat. For it is among their rules: the form of each element acts upon its matter essentially, and upon its neighbor by means of a quality, whether essential like the coldness of water, or accidental like its heat, active like heat and cold, or passive like moisture and dryness. And the matter of each element is acted upon essentially by its form and is qualified by the essential or accidental active or passive quality from the neighbor. And on this, what one objects to those who say that the agent is the form does not apply to those who say that it is the quality: the necessity of the passivity of the active quality when the breaking occurs between the two active ones, i.e., heat and cold, and the necessity of the activity of the passive quality when the breaking occurs between the two passive ones, i.e., moisture and dryness. For if it is said: If there is obscurity concerning the agency, there is no obscurity that that which is acted upon during mixture is the qualities, like the heat of fire and the coldness of water, and likewise the rest. We said: Yes, in the sense that they vanish and the intermediate quality occurs. But that which is affected and changes from one state to another is the matter alone. And just as its passivity is not impossible in the active quality like heat and cold, so the form's acting by the passive quality like moisture and dryness is not impossible, for it is certain that the form of water, for example, only breaks the dryness of fire by its wetness, not by its coldness, and the form of fire breaks the wetness of water by its dryness, not by its heat.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and objection-answer in a kalam discussion on mixture (imtizaj). The author begins by stating that the intensification and weakening of a quality simply means one quality is annihilated and another arises, determined by preparedness. The real dispute is about the agent: what breaks the original quality? Some say it is a simple form (the substantial form of one element) that breaks the quality of another. The author refutes this by first stating that it is not necessary that the breaker be a simple form; rather, the more plausible view is that the water form (the substantial form of water) breaks the coldness of the cold water through the medium of accidental heat (the heat that the water acquired when mixed with hot water). He then explains the rules underlying this: each elemental form acts on its own matter essentially and on its neighbor through a quality—either essential (like water's coldness) or accidental (like heat), and that quality can be active (heat/cold) or passive (moisture/dryness). The matter of each element is acted upon essentially by its own form and becomes qualified by the neighbor's quality. On this basis, the objection that raises contradictions for those who say the agent is the quality (i.e., the active quality itself) does not apply to those who say the agent is the form. Specifically, if the agent were the active quality, then when two active qualities (heat and cold) interact, the active quality would itself be passive, which is problematic; similarly, if an active quality were to act on a passive one, the passive would become active. But if the agent is the form, these problems do not arise because the form acts through an accidental quality. Then an objection is raised: even if the agent is obscure, it is clear that the passive subject in mixture is the qualities themselves (e.g., heat and cold are annihilated). The author answers: yes, the qualities vanish and an intermediate quality arises, but the thing that actually undergoes change from one state to another is the matter, not the qualities themselves. Just as matter can be passive to active qualities, it can also be the locus for the form's action through passive qualities. For example, water's form breaks fire's dryness by its own essential wetness, not by its coldness; fire's form breaks water's wetness by its own dryness, not by its heat.

فاعل
صورة
انكسار

Correction: The qualities vanish and an intermediate quality occurs, but the actual subject that is affected and changes from one state to another is the matter alone.

Checkpoint

A) The qualities themselves
B) The form of the element
C) The matter
D) The intermediate quality

Key Takeaway
The agent that breaks qualities in mixture is the substantial form acting through an accidental quality, and the matter is the real patient of change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a time you underwent a deep personal change. Was it merely an external 'quality' (a habit or action) that changed, or was it your inner 'form' (your essential character) that shifted? How does this lesson’s distinction between agent and patient help you understand the true source of lasting transformation in your life? What will you do to ensure your change is from your core?
?
The author argues that the patient of change is matter, not the qualities. In your spiritual journey, what is the 'matter' of your soul that must be reshaped? Are you too focused on acquiring and discarding superficial 'qualities' (e.g., performing rituals without reflection) while neglecting the essence that Allah wants to transform? Ask yourself honestly: what is the one deep-rooted trait you have been avoiding changing?
?
If the form acts through accidental qualities, then sometimes God uses unexpected means to break your harmful 'qualities' (like pride or indifference). Has there been a situation where a trial came through a seemingly unrelated channel (like a kind word from a stranger) that broke a negative pattern in you? How can you become more attentive to these subtle agents of change in your daily life, recognizing that their source is ultimately from Allah?

Definition of Similar Mixture Quality and Its Necessity
Sanusi defines the similarity of mixture quality and its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the similarity of mixture quality and why it requires a real uniform quality across all parts, not just perceptual similarity.

Core Idea
True mixture requires a real uniform quality in every part, not just appearance.

This passage from Sanusi clarifies one of the key concepts in natural philosophy: what it means for a mixture to have a similar quality throughout. He distinguishes true mixture from mere composition and explains why a genuine intermediate quality is necessary for the mixture to receive new forms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to get an overview of the definition and its implications.
Focus on the meaning of 'similarity' in this context.
2
Identify the definition
Find the sentence that defines the similarity of mixture quality. Note that it requires equality in specific reality across parts, differing only in location.
The fiery part is said to share heat, cold, etc., with the watery part.
3
Understand the consequence of lacking real similarity
Why does the author argue that mere perceptual similarity is insufficient? Because without a real intermediate quality, there is no action/passion and no preparation for new forms.
This connects to the philosophical principle that mixture must produce a new quality.
4
Distinguish mixture from composition
Note the author's distinction: mixture involves a new intermediate quality; composition is more general and may lack this. Check the examples and the reference to al-Shifa.
Also note that some scholars use 'ikhtilat' synonymously with 'imtizaj'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: أن معنى تشابه الكيفية المزاجية في الكل أن الحاصل في كل جزء من الأجزاء المركبة أو البسيطة للممتزج تماثل الحاصل في الجزء الآخر أي تساويه في الحقيقة النوعية من غير تفاوت إلا بالمحل، حتى أن الجزء الناري كالجزء المائي في الحرارة والبرودة والرطوبة واليبوسة وكذا الهوائي والأرضي، إذ لو اختلفت الكيفيات في أجزاء الممتزج وكان التشابه في الحس لشدة امتزاج الكيفيات العنصرية الباقية على حالها بحيث لا تتميز عند الحس لما كان هناك فعل وانفعال لم تتحقق كيفية وجودانية بها يستعد الممتزج لفيضان صورة معدنية أو نباتية أو حيوانية أو نفس إنسانية عليه بل كان هذا مجرد تركيب ومجاورة بين العناصر لا امتزاج لأن الامتزاج هو اجتماع العناصر بحيث تحدث منه الكيفية المتوسطة المتشابهة، والتركيب أعم من ذلك، وكذا الاختلاط وقد يجعل مرادفاً للامتزاج كذا في الشفاء، وما ذكر في شرح القانون من أن معنى التشابه في جميع الأجزاء أن يستحر بالقياس إلى البارد ويستبرد بالقياس إلى الحار وكذا في الرطوبة واليبوسة قصداً إلى دفع اعتراض الإمام بدخول توابع المزاج في تعريفه فمخالفة لصريح العقل وصحيح النقل، وما ذكرنا هو المفهوم من اللفظ والمذكور في كلام القوم. قال: فلا بد من استحالة العناصر في كيفياتها جميعاً. قد عرفت فيما مضى أن الكون والفساد تبدل في الصورة النوعية للعناصر.
The fourth: That the meaning of the similarity of the mixture quality in the whole is that what obtains in each part of the composite or simple parts of the mixture is similar to what obtains in the other part, i.e., it equals it in specific reality without difference except in location, such that the fiery part is like the watery part in heat, cold, moisture, and dryness, and likewise the airy and earthy. For if the qualities differed in the parts of the mixture and the similarity were perceptual due to the intensity of the mixing of the elemental qualities remaining in their state such that they are not distinguished by sense, then there would be no action and passion, and an existential quality would not be realized by which the mixture becomes prepared for the influx of a mineral, plant, animal, or human soul form. Rather, this would be mere composition and adjacency between the elements, not mixture, because mixture is the joining of elements such that the intermediate similar quality arises from it, and composition is more general than that, and likewise mixing, and it may be made synonymous with mixture, as in al-Shifa. And what was mentioned in Sharh al-Qanun, that the meaning of similarity in all parts is that it is hot relative to the cold and cold relative to the hot, and likewise for moisture and dryness, aiming to repel the Imam's objection regarding the inclusion of concomitant accidents of mixture in its definition, is contrary to clear reason and sound transmission. And what we have mentioned is the meaning understood from the expression and mentioned in the speech of the authorities. He said: So there must be transformation of the elements in all their qualities. You have already known earlier that generation and corruption are a change in the specific form of the elements.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage contains the fourth point in a classification of issues related to mixture. It defines what is meant by the similarity of the mixture quality (al-kayfiyya al-mizajiyya) across all parts. The definition: the quality present in every part of the mixture (whether composite or simple) is similar in specific reality to the quality in every other part, with no difference except in the particular substance (location). For example, the fiery part shares the same heat, cold, moisture, and dryness as the watery part. The author then explains the consequence if qualities were merely perceptually similar due to fine mixing while remaining unchanged: there would be no real action and passion, and no genuine intermediate quality would arise. Without such a quality, the mixture could not receive a new mineral, plant, animal, or human soul form—it would be mere juxtaposition (tarkib) and adjacency (mujawara), not true mixture (imtizaj). The author distinguishes mixture from composition and mixing (ikhtilat), though some make them synonymous. He then criticizes a definition given in Sharh al-Qanun, which defined similarity relative to hot/cold and moist/dry, as contrary to reason and transmitted knowledge. Finally, he quotes the original text (matn): 'So there must be transformation of the elements in all their qualities.' The commentator then reminds that generation and corruption (kawn wa fasad) involve a change in the specific form of the elements.

Key Terms
كيفية مزاجية
تشابه
امتزاج
تركيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that perceptual similarity due to fine mixing is sufficient for a true mixture.
Correction: The author argues that without a real uniform quality, there is no genuine mixture; the elements must produce a new intermediate quality.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what distinguishes true mixture (imtizaj) from mere composition (tarkib)?
A) In mixture, the elements remain unchanged
B) In mixture, a new intermediate similar quality arises from the combination
C) In composition, the elements lose their identities
D) There is no difference; the terms are synonymous

Key Takeaway
True mixture requires a real uniform quality in every part arising from the interaction of elements, not just perceptual similarity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, you learned that mere perceptual similarity without a real inner change is insufficient for true mixture. Consider your own spiritual life: are you content with a 'perceptual' faith—practices that look good to others—while your inner qualities remain unchanged? What specific area of your character might still retain its 'original elemental selfishness' rather than being transformed into a new, uniform sincerity in seeking Allah?
?
The passage warns that without a genuine existential quality, the mixture cannot receive a higher form (like a human soul). Reflect: if your soul is meant to be a mixture of body and spirit prepared to receive divine grace, what 'perceptual similarities' (e.g., outward piety) might be masking the absence of real transformation? What one action will you take today to move from 'composition' —a list of good deeds—to 'mixture'—where every part of your life is uniformly animated by the remembrance of Allah?
